**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api`, `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd`

# Kubernetes Scheduler Plugin Framework Architecture

## Your Task

A new Kubernetes contributor wants to understand the scheduler plugin framework architecture. Find the key Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the scheduling framework: 1. The framework interface definitions (Plugin, FilterPlugin, ScorePlugin, BindPlugin, etc. in pkg/scheduler/framework/). 2. The ScheduleOne orchestration function that drives the scheduling cycle for a single pod. 3. The top-level Scheduler struct and its Run method. 4. The frameworkImpl runtime that invokes plugins (RunFilterPlugins, RunScorePlugins). 5. The plugin registry and the NewInTreeRegistry that registers all built-in plugins. Report each file path and key symbols.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the onboarding domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Summary

I've identified and documented **6 key files** and **33+ critical symbols** that implement the scheduler plugin framework:

### Key Components Found:

1. **Framework Interface Definitions** (`pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go`)
   - Parent `Plugin` interface
   - 13 specific plugin interfaces (PreEnqueue, Filter, Score, Bind, etc.)
   - `Status` and `WaitingPod` types

2. **ScheduleOne Orchestration** (`pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go`)
   - `ScheduleOne()`: Orchestrates the entire scheduling workflow
   - `schedulingCycle()`: Runs filter, score, reserve, and permit plugins
   - `bindingCycle()`: Runs bind and post-bind plugins

3. **Top-Level Scheduler** (`pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go`)
   - `Scheduler` struct with cache, queue, and profiles
   - `Run()` method: Starts the scheduler loop in a goroutine

4. **frameworkImpl Runtime** (`pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go`)
   - `frameworkImpl` struct with plugin lists for each extension point
   - `RunFilterPlugins()`: Sequential filter execution
   - `RunScorePlugins()`: Parallel scoring with normalization
   - 8+ other plugin invocation methods for all extension points

5. **Plugin Registry** (`pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go` and `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/registry.go`)
   - `Registry` type: Map of plugin names to factories
   - `NewInTreeRegistry()`: Registers 18+ built-in plugins

Scheduler Plugin Framework Architecture\\n\\n### Framework Interface Definitions\\nThe core framework interfaces are defined in **pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go**. The parent interface **Plugin** is the base for all scheduling framework plugins. Key plugin interfaces include:\\n\\n- **PreEnqueuePlugin**: Called before adding pods to activeQ\\n- **QueueSortPlugin**: Used to sort pods in the scheduling queue\\n- **PreFilterPlugin**: Called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle; can pre-compute and optionally filter candidate nodes\\n- **FilterPlugin**: Filters out nodes that cannot run a pod\\n- **PostFilterPlugin**: Called when a pod cannot be scheduled (enables preemption logic)\\n- **PreScorePlugin**: Informational extension point after filtering passes\\n- **ScorePlugin**: Scores nodes based on criteria; implements **ScoreExtensions** for normalization\\n- **ReservePlugin**: Reserves resources for a pod\\n- **PermitPlugin**: Permits or denies pod binding\\n- **PreBindPlugin**: Pre-bind logic before binding\\n- **BindPlugin**: Binds the pod to a node\\n- **PostBindPlugin**: Post-bind logic\\n\\nThe **Status** struct and **WaitingPod** interface are also defined here to represent plugin execution results and permit-phase state.\\n\\n### ScheduleOne Orchestration Function\\nThe function **func (sched *Scheduler) ScheduleOne(ctx context.Context)** in **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** is the main orchestration function that drives the scheduling cycle for a single pod. It:\\n\\n1. Retrieves the next pod from the scheduling queue\\n2. Selects the appropriate framework (scheduler profile) for the pod\\n3. Calls **schedulingCycle()** to attempt scheduling the pod\\n4. On success, asynchronously calls **bindingCycle()** to bind the pod\\n\\nThe **schedulingCycle()** function calls the actual scheduler's **SchedulePod()** method, which invokes the framework plugins through multiple extension points.\\n\\nThe **bindingCycle()** function handles the actual binding and post-bind operations.\\n\\n### Top-Level Scheduler Struct and Run Method\\nThe **Scheduler** struct in **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** is the top-level component with the following key fields:\\n\\n- **Cache**: Internal cache of node and pod state\\n- **NextPod**: Function to retrieve the next pod to schedule from the queue\\n- **FailureHandler**: Called upon scheduling failure\\n- **SchedulePod**: Function that invokes the scheduling algorithm through framework plugins\\n- **SchedulingQueue**: Holds pods to be scheduled\\n- **Profiles**: Map of scheduler profiles (each with its own framework)\\n\\nThe **func (sched *Scheduler) Run(ctx context.Context)** method in **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** is the entry point that:\\n\\n1. Starts the SchedulingQueue\\n2. Launches a goroutine running **ScheduleOne** in a loop via **wait.UntilWithContext()**\\n3. Blocks until context is done, then closes the queue and plugins\\n\\n### frameworkImpl Runtime\\nThe **frameworkImpl** struct in **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go** is the component responsible for initializing and running scheduler plugins. It contains:\\n\\n- Lists of plugin implementations for each extension point (preEnqueuePlugins, filterPlugins, scorePlugins, etc.)\\n- A plugin registry and metrics recording\\n- Methods to run plugins at each extension point\\n\\nKey plugin invocation methods:\\n\\n- **RunPreFilterPlugins()**: Runs pre-filter plugins\\n- **RunFilterPlugins()**: Runs filter plugins on a node; returns first failure\\n- **RunPostFilterPlugins()**: Runs post-filter plugins for preemption logic\\n- **RunPreScorePlugins()**: Runs pre-score plugins\\n- **RunScorePlugins()**: Runs scoring plugins in parallel on all nodes, normalizes scores, and applies weights\\n- **RunReservePluginsReserve()**: Reserves resources\\n- **RunPreBindPlugins()**: Pre-bind plugins\\n- **RunBindPlugins()**: Bind plugins to attach pod to node\\n- **RunPostBindPlugins()**: Post-bind plugins\\n- **RunPermitPlugins()**: Permit plugins for final approval\\n\\nThese methods implement the complete plugin execution orchestration, including parallelization, metrics recording, and error handling.\\n\\n### Plugin Registry and NewInTreeRegistry\\nThe **Registry** type in **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go** is a map from plugin name to **PluginFactory** function. It provides methods to register, unregister, and merge plugins.\\n\\n**PluginFactory** is a function signature for building a plugin:\\n```go\\ntype PluginFactory = func(ctx context.Context, configuration runtime.Object, f framework.Handle) (framework.Plugin, error)\\n```\\n\\n**PluginFactoryWithFts** allows injecting feature gates:\\n```go\\ntype PluginFactoryWithFts func(context.Context, runtime.Object, framework.Handle, plfeature.Features) (framework.Plugin, error)\\n```\\n\\nThe **func NewInTreeRegistry() runtime.Registry** function in **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/registry.go** builds the registry with all in-tree plugins:\\n\\n- dynamicresources\\n- imagelocality\\n- tainttoleration\\n- nodename\\n- nodeports\\n- nodeaffinity\\n- podtopologyspread\\n- nodeunschedulable\\n- noderesources (Fit and BalancedAllocation)\\n- volumebinding\\n- volumerestrictions\\n- volumezone\\n- nodevolumelimits (CSI)\\n- interpodaffinity\\n- queuesort (PrioritySort)\\n- defaultbinder\\n- defaultpreemption\\n- schedulinggates\\n\\nOut-of-tree plugins can be registered via the **WithFrameworkOutOfTreeRegistry** option passed to the scheduler.\\n\\n### Summary\\nThe scheduler framework provides a plugin-based architecture where:\\n1. **Scheduler.Run()** starts the scheduling loop\\n2. **ScheduleOne()** coordinates the scheduling of individual pods\\n3. **schedulingCycle()** invokes the framework plugins through multiple extension points\\n4. **frameworkImpl** executes each plugin interface at designated extension points\\n5. **Registry** maintains all available plugins (in-tree and out-of-tree)\\n6. Each plugin interface enables different aspects of the scheduling decision (filtering, scoring, binding, etc.)\\n\"\n}\n",
